plainlands</span>\n</td>\n<td>506</td>\n<td>34.8</td>\n<td>23.7\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left">Mandera\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><span style="font-size:90%;">Dry north plainlands</span>\n</td>\n<td>506</td>\n<td>34.8</td>\n<td>25.7\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Kenya" title="Wildlife of Kenya">Wildlife of Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Kenya" title="Environmental issues in Kenya">Environmental issues in Kenya</a></div>\n<p>Kenya has considerable land area devoted to <a href="/wiki/Wildlife" title="Wildlife">wildlife</a> habitats, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masai_Mara" title="Masai Mara">Masai Mara</a>, where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_Wildebeest" title="Blue Wildebeest">blue wildebeest</a> and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bovid" title="Bovid">bovids</a> participate in a large scale <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/migration" title="wikt:migration">annual migration</a>. More than 1 million wildebeest and 200,000 zebras participate in the migration across the <a href="/wiki/Mara_River" title="Mara River">Mara River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Five_Game" title="Big Five Game">"Big Five"</a> game animals of Africa, that is the <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_buffalo" title="African buffalo">buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceros</a>, and <a href="/wiki/African_elephant" title="African elephant">elephant</a>, can be found in Kenya and in the Masai Mara in particular. A significant population of other wild animals, reptiles and birds can be found in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Kenya" title="List of national parks of Kenya">national parks</a> and game reserves in the country. The annual animal migration occurs between June and September with millions of animals taking part, attracting valuable foreign tourism. Two million wildebeest migrate a distance of 2,900 kilometres (1,802&#160;mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Serengeti" title="Serengeti">Serengeti</a> in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> to the Masai Mara<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> in Kenya, in a constant clockwise fashion, searching for food and water supplies. This Serengeti Migration of the wildebeest is a curious spectacle listed among the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Natural_Wonders_of_Africa" title="Seven Natural Wonders of Africa">Seven Natural Wonders of Africa</a>.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Kenya" title="Politics of Kenya">Politics of Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mwai_Kibaki,_October_2003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="175" data-file-width="150" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/Mwai_Kibaki%2C_October_2003.jpg" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mwai_Kibaki,_October_2003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenya\'s third president <a href="/wiki/Mwai_Kibaki" title="Mwai Kibaki">Mwai Kibaki</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic. The president is both the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and of a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Kenya" title="National Assembly of Kenya">National Assembly</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Kenya" title="Senate of Kenya">Senate</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. There was growing concern especially during former president Daniel arap Moi\'s tenure that the executive was increasingly meddling with the affairs of the judiciary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenya has a high degree of corruption according to <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corruption_Perception_Index" title="Corruption Perception Index">Corruption Perception Index</a> (CPI), a metric which attempts to gauge the prevalence of public sector corruption in various countries. In 2012, the nation placed 139th out of 176 total countries in the CPI, with a score of 27/100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TICPI_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-TICPI-95">[95]</a></sup> However, there are several rather significant developments with regards to curbing corruption from the Kenyan government, for instance, the establishment of a new and independent Ethics and Anti-Corruption Commission (EACC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JUDICIARY.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3672" data-file-width="4896" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JUDICIARY.JPG/220px-JUDICIARY.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JUDICIARY.JPG/330px-JUDICIARY.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JUDICIARY.JPG/440px-JUDICIARY.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JUDICIARY.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Kenya" title="Supreme Court of Kenya">Supreme Court of Kenya</a> building.</div></div></div>\n<p>Following general elections held in 1997, the Constitution of Kenya Review Act designed to pave the way for more comprehensive amendments to the Kenyan constitution was passed by the national parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2002, Kenyans held democratic and open elections, most of which were judged free and fair by international observers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The 2002 elections marked an important turning point in Kenya\'s democratic evolution in that power was transferred peacefully from the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_African_National_Union" title="Kenya African National Union">Kenya African National Union</a> (KANU), which had ruled the country since independence to the <a href="/wiki/National_Rainbow_Coalition" title="National Rainbow Coalition">National Rainbow Coalition</a> (NARC), a coalition of political parties.\n</p><p>Under the presidency of <a href="/wiki/Mwai_Kibaki" title="Mwai Kibaki">Mwai Kibaki</a>, the new ruling coalition promised to focus its efforts on generating economic growth, combating corruption, improving education, and rewriting its constitution. A few of these promises have been met. There is free primary education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In 2007, the government issued a statement declaring that from 2008, secondary education would be heavily subsidised, with the government footing all tuition fees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_elections_and_new_government">2013 elections and new government</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenyan_general_election,_2013" title="Kenyan general election, 2013">Kenyan general election, 2013</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenyan_local_elections,_2013" title="Kenyan local elections, 2013">Kenyan local elections, 2013</a></div>\n<p>Under the new constitution and with President Kibaki prohibited by term limits from running for a third term, Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">Uhuru Kenyatta</a> ran for office. He won with 50.51% of the vote in March 2013.\n</p><p>In December 2014, President <a href="/wiki/Uhuru_Kenyatta" title="Uhuru Kenyatta">Uhuru Kenyatta</a> signed a Security Laws Amendment Bill, which supporters of the law suggested was necessary to guard against armed groups. Opposition politicians, human rights groups, and nine Western countries criticised the security bill, arguing that it infringed on democratic freedoms. The governments of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> also collectively issued a press statement cautioning about the law\'s potential impact. Through the Jubilee Coalition, the Bill was later passed on 19 December in the National Assembly under acrimonious circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kenya" title="Foreign relations of Kenya">Foreign relations of Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_(20848405843).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="980" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg/220px-President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg/330px-President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg/440px-President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_%2820848405843%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_visits_Nairobi_Kenya_July_2015_(20848405843).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in Nairobi, July 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya has close ties with its fellow <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>-speaking neighbours in the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a> region. Relations with Uganda and Tanzania are generally strong, as the three nations work toward economic and social integration through common membership in the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a>.\n</p><p>Relations with Somalia have historically been tense, although there has been some military co-ordination against Islamist insurgents. Kenya has good relations with the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upenn_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-upenn-102">[102]</a></sup> Kenya is one of the most pro-American nations in Africa, and the wider world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>With <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> trial dates scheduled in 2013 for both President Kenyatta and Deputy President <a href="/wiki/William_Ruto" title="William Ruto">William Ruto</a> related to the 2007 election aftermath, US president <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> chose not to visit the country during his <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_visits_to_Sub-Saharan_Africa#List_of_trips" title="United States presidential visits to Sub-Saharan Africa">mid-2013 African trip</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Later in the summer, Kenyatta visited China at the invitation of President <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a> after a stop in Russia and not having visited the United States as president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp01_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-wp01-105">[105]</a></sup> In July 2015 Obama visited Kenya, the first American president to visit the country while in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Defence_Forces" title="Kenya Defence Forces">Kenya Defence Forces</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer,_Leonard_Ngondi,_left,_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols,_left,_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer%2C_Leonard_Ngondi%2C_left%2C_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols%2C_left%2C_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer%2C_Leonard_Ngondi%2C_left%2C_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols%2C_left%2C_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer%2C_Leonard_Ngondi%2C_left%2C_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols%2C_left%2C_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_060806-N-0411D-109_Kenyan_Army_Brig._Gen._and_Natural_Fire_Commanding_Officer,_Leonard_Ngondi,_left,_greets_U.S._Marine_Lt._Col._Steve_Nichols,_left,_at_Camp_Lonestar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenyan Army Brig. Gen. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Leonard_Muriuki_Ngondi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Leonard Muriuki Ngondi (page does not exist)">Leonard Ngondi</a>, left,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> greets U.S. Marine Lt. Col. Steve Nichols, left, at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Camp_Lonestar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Camp Lonestar (page does not exist)">Camp Lonestar</a> in Kenya, 2006</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>Kenya Defence Forces</b> are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armed_forces" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Kenya" title="Republic of Kenya">Republic of Kenya</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Army" title="Kenya Army">Kenya Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Navy" title="Kenya Navy">Kenya Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Air_Force" title="Kenya Air Force">Kenya Air Force</a> compose the National Defence Forces. The current Kenya Defence Forces were established, and its composition laid out, in Article 241 of the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kenya" title="Constitution of Kenya">Constitution of Kenya</a>; the KDF is governed by the Kenya Defence Forces Act of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Kenya" title="President of Kenya">President of Kenya</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of all the armed forces.\n</p><p>The armed forces are regularly deployed in peacekeeping missions around the world. Further, in the aftermath of the national elections of December 2007 and the violence that subsequently engulfed the country, a commission of inquiry, the <a href="/wiki/Waki_Commission" title="Waki Commission">Waki Commission</a>, commended its readiness and adjudged it to "have performed its duty well."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Nevertheless, there have been serious allegations of human rights violations, most recently while conducting counter-insurgency operations in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt_Elgon" title="Mt Elgon">Mt Elgon</a> area<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> and also in the district of <a href="/wiki/Mandera" title="Mandera">Mandera</a> central.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="804" data-file-width="620" decoding="async" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif/220px-Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif/330px-Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif/440px-Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_showing_Counties_underthe_new_kenyan_constitution..gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenya\'s <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">47 counties</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya\'s armed forces, like many government institutions in the country, have been tainted by <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Kenya" title="Corruption in Kenya">corruption</a> allegations. Because the operations of the armed forces have been traditionally cloaked by the ubiquitous blanket of "state security", the corruption has been hidden from public view, and thus less subject to public scrutiny and notoriety. This has changed recently. In what are by Kenyan standards unprecedented revelations, in 2010, credible claims of corruption were made with regard to recruitment <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> and procurement of Armoured Personnel Carriers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Further, the wisdom and prudence of certain decisions of procurement have been publicly questioned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">Counties of Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Divisions_of_Kenya" title="Divisions of Kenya">Divisions of Kenya</a></div>\n<p>Kenya is divided into <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">47 semi-autonomous counties</a> that are headed by governors. These 47 counties now form the first-order divisions of Kenya.\n</p><p>The smallest administrative units in Kenya are called <a href="/wiki/Locations_of_Kenya" title="Locations of Kenya">locations</a>. Locations often coincide with electoral wards. Locations are usually named after their central villages/towns. Many larger towns consist of several locations. Each location has a chief, appointed by the state.\n</p><p>Constituencies are an electoral subdivision, with each county comprising a whole number of constituencies. An Interim Boundaries commission was formed in year 2010 to review the constituencies and in its report, it recommended creation of an additional 80 constituencies. Previous to the 2013 elections, there were 210 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Kenya" title="Constituencies of Kenya">constituencies in Kenya</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kenya" title="Human rights in Kenya">Human rights in Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Kenya" title="LGBT rights in Kenya">LGBT rights in Kenya</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">Homosexual acts</a> are illegal in Kenya and punishable by up to 14 years in prison though the state often turns a blind eye on prosecuting homosexuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> According to 2013 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 90% of Kenyans believe that homosexuality should not be accepted by society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewglobal.org_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-pewglobal.org-117">[117]</a></sup> While addressing a joint press conference together with President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in 2015, President Kenyatta declined to assure Kenya\'s commitment to gay rights saying that "the issue of gay rights is really a non-issue."  "But there are some things that we must admit we don\'t share. Our culture, our societies don\'t accept." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2008, <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> brought wide international attention<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> to <i>The Cry of Blood</i> report. In the report, the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_National_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="Kenya National Commission on Human Rights">Kenya National Commission on Human Rights</a> (KNCHR) reported these in their key finding "e)", stating that the <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">forced disappearances</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_killing" title="Extrajudicial killing">extrajudicial killings</a> appeared to be official policy sanctioned by the political leadership, the Police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The police often shoot suspected gangsters in public as a new "strategy" to fight the rising levels of crime in the country in total disregard of the laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kenya" title="Economy of Kenya">Economy of Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Export_Treemap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2086" data-file-width="2668" decoding="async" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kenya_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Kenya_Export_Treemap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kenya_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Kenya_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kenya_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Kenya_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Export_Treemap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Kenya\'s exports.</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya has a <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) of 0.555(medium), ranked 145 out of 186 in the world. As of  2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kenya&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 17.7% of Kenyans lived on less than $1.25 a day. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELudeki_ChweyaJohn_Kithome_TutaS._Kichamu_Akivaga2005_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELudeki_ChweyaJohn_Kithome_TutaS._Kichamu_Akivaga2005-122">[122]</a></sup> In 2017, Kenya ranked 92nd in the World Bank <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">ease of doing business</a> rating from 113rd in 2016 (of 190 countries).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The important agricultural sector is one of the least developed and largely inefficient, employing 75% of the workforce compared to less than 3% in the <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food secure</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_countries" title="Developed countries">developed countries</a>.  Kenya is usually classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frontier_market" title="Frontier market">frontier market</a> or occasionally an <a href="/wiki/Emerging_market" title="Emerging market">emerging market</a>, but it is not one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" title="Least developed countries">least developed countries</a>.\n</p><p>The economy has seen much expansion, seen by strong performance in tourism, higher education and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Kenya" title="Telecommunications in Kenya">telecommunications</a>, and acceptable<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view"><span title="This statement is possibly biased. (January 2015)">neutrality</span></a> is <a href="/wiki/Talk:Kenya" title="Talk:Kenya">disputed</a></i>]</sup> post-drought results in agriculture, especially the vital tea sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-124">[124]</a></sup> Kenya\'s economy grew by more than 7% in 2007, and its foreign debt was greatly reduced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-124">[124]</a></sup> But this changed immediately after the disputed presidential election of December 2007, following the chaos which engulfed the country.\n</p><p>Telecommunication and financial activity over the last decade now comprises 62% of GDP. 22% of GDP still comes from the unreliable agricultural sector which employs 75% of the labour force (a consistent characteristic of under-developed economies that have not attained <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>&#8212;an important catalyst of economic growth) A small portion of the population relies on food aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-125">[125]</a></sup> Industry and manufacturing is the smallest sector, accounting for 16% of GDP.  The service, industry and manufacturing sectors only employ 25% of the labour force but contribute 75% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_124-2"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-124">[124]</a></sup>\nKenya also exports textiles worth over $400million under Agoa.\n</p><p>Privatisation of state corporations like the defunct Kenya Post and Telecommunications Company, which resulted in East Africa\'s most profitable company&#8212;<a href="/wiki/Safaricom" title="Safaricom">Safaricom</a>, has led to their revival because of massive private investment.\n</p><p>As of  May&#160;2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kenya&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, economic prospects are positive with 4&#8211;5% GDP growth expected, largely because of expansions in <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a>, transport, construction and a recovery in <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> estimated growth of 4.3% in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldBanki_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-WorldBanki-126">[126]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenya,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="188" data-file-width="441" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Kenya%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/350px-Kenya%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/Kenya%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenya,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenya, Trends in the Human Development Index 1970&#8211;2010.</div></div></div>\n<p>In March 1996, the presidents of Kenya, Tanzania, and Uganda re-established the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> (EAC). The EAC\'s objectives include harmonising tariffs and customs regimes, free movement of people, and improving regional infrastructures. In March 2004, the three East African countries signed a <a href="/wiki/Customs_union" title="Customs union">Customs Union Agreement</a>.\n</p><p>Kenya is East and Central Africa\'s hub for financial services. The <a href="/wiki/Nairobi_Securities_Exchange" title="Nairobi Securities Exchange">Nairobi Securities Exchange</a> (NSE) is ranked 4th in Africa in terms of market capitalisation. The Kenyan banking system is supervised by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Kenya" title="Central Bank of Kenya">Central Bank of Kenya</a> (CBK). As of late July 2004, the system consisted of 43 commercial banks (down from 48 in 2001), several <a href="/wiki/Non-bank_financial_institution" title="Non-bank financial institution">non-bank financial institutions</a>, including mortgage companies, four savings and loan associations, and several core foreign-exchange bureaus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_124-3"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-124">[124]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kenya" title="Tourism in Kenya">Tourism in Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg/220px-Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg/330px-Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg/440px-Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elephants_at_Amboseli_national_park_against_Mount_Kilimanjaro.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amboseli_National_Park" title="Amboseli National Park">Amboseli National Park</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2433" data-file-width="6986" decoding="async" height="77" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg/220px-Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg/330px-Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg/440px-Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tsavo_east_panorama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tsavo_East_National_Park" title="Tsavo East National Park">Tsavo East National Park</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kenya" title="Tourism in Kenya">Tourism in Kenya</a> is the second-largest source of foreign exchange revenue following agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>  The Kenya Tourism Board is responsible for maintaining information pertaining to tourism in Kenya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>\nThe main tourist attractions are photo safaris through the <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Kenya" title="List of national parks of Kenya">60 national parks</a> and game reserves. Other attractions include the wildebeest migration at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masaai_Mara" title="Masaai Mara">Masaai Mara</a> which is considered the 7th wonder of the world, historical mosques and colonial-era forts at <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malindi" title="Malindi">Malindi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lamu" title="Lamu">Lamu</a>; the renowned vast scenery like the snow white capped <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kenya" title="Mount Kenya">Mount Kenya</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley,_Kenya" title="Great Rift Valley, Kenya">Great Rift Valley</a>;  the tea plantations at <a href="/wiki/Kericho" title="Kericho">Kericho</a>; the coffee plantations at <a href="/wiki/Thika" title="Thika">Thika</a>; a splendid view of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt._Kilimanjaro" title="Mt. Kilimanjaro">Mt. Kilimanjaro</a> across the border into <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ne_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-ne-130">[130]</a></sup> and the beaches along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swahili_Coast" title="Swahili Coast">Swahili Coast</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>. Tourists, the largest number being from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, are attracted mainly to the coastal beaches and the <a href="/wiki/Game_reserve" title="Game reserve">game reserves</a>, notably, the expansive <a href="/wiki/Tsavo_East_National_Park" title="Tsavo East National Park">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tsavo_West_National_Park" title="Tsavo West National Park">Tsavo West National Park</a> 20,808 square kilometres (8,034&#160;sq&#160;mi) in the southeast.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Kenya" title="Agriculture in Kenya">Agriculture in Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2794" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG/220px-Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG/330px-Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG/440px-Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenya-Tealand-Near-Kericho-2012.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Tea farm near <a href="/wiki/Kericho" title="Kericho">Kericho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kericho_County" title="Kericho County">Kericho County</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Agriculture is the second largest contributor to Kenya\'s gross domestic product (GDP), after the service sector. In 2005 agriculture, including <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a> and fishing, accounted for 24% of GDP, as well as for 18% of wage employment and 50% of revenue from exports. The principal <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crops</a> are tea, horticultural produce, and coffee. Horticultural produce and tea are the main growth sectors and the two most valuable of all of Kenya\'s exports. The production of major food staples such as <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a> is subject to sharp weather-related fluctuations. Production downturns periodically necessitate food aid&#8212;for example, in 2004 aid for 1.8&#160;million people because of one of Kenya\'s intermittent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Droughts" title="Droughts">droughts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A consortium led by the <a href="/wiki/International_Crops_Research_Institute_for_the_Semi-Arid_Tropics" title="International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics">International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICRISAT" title="ICRISAT">ICRISAT</a>) has had some success in helping farmers grow new <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_pea" title="Pigeon pea">pigeon pea</a> varieties, instead of maize, in particularly dry areas. Pigeon peas are very drought resistant, so can be grown in areas with less than 650&#160;mm annual rainfall. Successive projects encouraged the commercialisation of legumes, by stimulating the growth of local seed production and agro-dealer networks for distribution and marketing. This work, which included linking producers to wholesalers, helped to increase local producer prices by 20&#8211;25% in Nairobi and Mombasa. The commercialisation of the pigeon pea is now enabling some farmers to buy assets, ranging from mobile phones to productive land and livestock, and is opening pathways for them to move out of poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tea, coffee, sisal, pyrethrum, corn, and wheat are grown in the fertile highlands, one of the most successful agricultural production regions in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-91">[91]</a></sup> Livestock predominates in the semi-arid savanna to the north and east. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coconuts" title="Coconuts">Coconuts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pineapples" title="Pineapples">pineapples</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cashew_nuts" title="Cashew nuts">cashew nuts</a>, cotton, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sisal" title="Sisal">sisal</a>, and corn are grown in the lower-lying areas. Kenya has not attained the level of investment and efficiency in agriculture that can guarantee food security and coupled with resulting poverty (53% of the population lives below the poverty line), a significant portion of the population regularly starves and is heavily dependent on food aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-125">[125]</a></sup> Poor roads, an inadequate railway network, under-used water transport and expensive air transport have isolated mostly <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-arid" title="Semi-arid">semi-arid</a> areas and farmers in other regions often leave food to rot in the fields because they cannot access markets. This was last seen in August and September 2011 prompting the <a href="/wiki/Kenyans_for_Kenya" title="Kenyans for Kenya">Kenyans for Kenya</a> initiative by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kapsowar1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kapsowar1.JPG/220px-Kapsowar1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kapsowar1.JPG/330px-Kapsowar1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kapsowar1.JPG/440px-Kapsowar1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kapsowar1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Agricultural countryside in Kenya</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya\'s <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> sector is categorized into three organizational types: smallholder schemes, centrally-managed public schemes and private/commercial irrigation schemes.\n</p><p>The smallholder schemes are owned, developed and managed by individuals or groups of farmers operating as water users or self-help groups. Irrigation is carried out on individual or on group farms averaging 0.1&#8211;0.4 ha. There are about 3,000 smallholder irrigation schemes covering a total area of 47,000 ha.\nThe country has seven large, centrally managed irrigation schemes, namely Mwea, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bura_irrigation_and_Settlement_Project_(Kenya)" title="Bura irrigation and Settlement Project (Kenya)">Bura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hola,_Kenya" title="Hola, Kenya">Hola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perkerra_River" title="Perkerra River">Perkera</a>, West Kano, Bunyala and <a href="/wiki/Ahero" title="Ahero">Ahero</a> covering a total commanded area of 18,200 ha and averaging 2,600 ha per scheme. These schemes are managed by the National Irrigation Board and account for 18% of irrigated land area in Kenya.\nLarge-scale private commercial farms cover 45,000 hectares accounting for 40% of irrigated land. They utilize high technology and produce high-value crops for the export market, especially flowers and vegetables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenya is the world\'s 3rd largest exporter of <a href="/wiki/Cut_flowers" title="Cut flowers">cut flowers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kenya-flower-industry_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-kenya-flower-industry-135">[135]</a></sup> Roughly half of Kenya\'s 127 flower farms are concentrated around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Naivasha" title="Lake Naivasha">Lake Naivasha</a>, 90 kilometers northwest of Nairobi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kenya-flower-industry_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-kenya-flower-industry-135">[135]</a></sup> To speed their export, Nairobi airport has a terminal dedicated to the transport of flowers and vegetables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kenya-flower-industry_135-2"><a href="#cite_note-kenya-flower-industry-135">[135]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_manufacturing">Industry and manufacturing</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2269" data-file-width="6152" decoding="async" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg/300px-Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg/450px-Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg/600px-Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orrling_of_Nairobi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenya_Commercial_Bank" title="Kenya Commercial Bank">Kenya Commercial Bank</a> headquarters at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=KENCOM_House&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="KENCOM House (page does not exist)">KENCOM House</a> (right) in Nairobi.</div></div></div>\n<p>Although Kenya is the most industrially developed country in the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a> region, manufacturing still accounts for only 14% of the GDP. Industrial activity, concentrated around the three largest urban centres, <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kisumu" title="Kisumu">Kisumu</a>, is dominated by food-processing industries such as grain milling, beer production, and sugarcane crushing, and the fabrication of consumer goods, e.g., vehicles from kits.\n</p><p>There is a cement production industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Kenya has an <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refinery</a> that processes imported crude petroleum into petroleum products, mainly for the domestic market. In addition, a substantial and expanding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Informal_sector" title="Informal sector">informal sector</a> commonly referred to as <i>jua kali</i> engages in small-scale manufacturing of household goods, auto parts, and farm implements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenya\'s inclusion among the beneficiaries of the US Government\'s African Growth and Opportunity Act (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AGOA" title="AGOA">AGOA</a>) has given a boost to manufacturing in recent years. Since AGOA took effect in 2000, Kenya\'s clothing sales to the United States increased from US$44&#160;million to US$270&#160;million (2006).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Other initiatives to strengthen manufacturing have been the new government\'s favourable tax measures, including the removal of duty on capital equipment and other raw materials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kenya" title="Transport in Kenya">Transport in Kenya</a></div>\n<p>The country has an extensive network of paved and unpaved roads. Kenya\'s railway system links the nation\'s ports and major cities, connecting it with neighbouring Uganda. There are 15 airports which have paved runways.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Kenya" title="Energy in Kenya">Energy in Kenya</a></div>\n<p>The largest share of Kenya\'s electricity supply comes from geothermal energy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> followed by hydroelectric stations at dams along the upper <a href="/wiki/Tana_River_(Kenya)" title="Tana River (Kenya)">Tana River</a>, as well as the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Turkwel_Gorge_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Turkwel Gorge Dam (page does not exist)">Turkwel Gorge Dam</a> in the west. A petroleum-fired plant on the coast, <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_power_in_Kenya" title="Geothermal power in Kenya">geothermal facilities</a> at <a href="/wiki/Olkaria" title="Olkaria">Olkaria</a> (near Nairobi), and electricity imported from <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> make up the rest of the supply. Kenya\'s installed capacity stood at 1,142 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megawatts" title="Megawatts">megawatts</a> between 2001 and 2003. The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Electricity_Generating_Company" title="Kenya Electricity Generating Company">Kenya Electricity Generating Company (KenGen)</a>, established in 1997 under the name of Kenya Power Company, handles the generation of electricity, while Kenya Power handles the electricity transmission and distribution system in the country. Shortfalls of electricity occur periodically, when drought reduces water flow. To become energy sufficient, Kenya aims to build a nuclear power plant by 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg/170px-Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg/255px-Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg/340px-Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Worker_in_Olkaria_Kenya.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Workers at <a href="/wiki/Olkaria_II_Geothermal_Power_Station" title="Olkaria II Geothermal Power Station">Olkaria Geothermal Power Plant</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya has proven deposits of oil in <a href="/wiki/Turkana_County" title="Turkana County">Turkana</a> and the commercial viability was just discovered. <a href="/wiki/Tullow_Oil" title="Tullow Oil">Tullow Oil</a> estimates Kenya\'s oil reserves to be around 10 billion barrels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Exploration is still continuing to determine if there are more reserves. Kenya currently imports all crude petroleum requirements. Kenya, east Africa\'s largest economy, has no strategic reserves and relies solely on oil marketers\' 21-day oil reserves required under industry regulations. Petroleum accounts for 20% to 25% of the national import bill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overall_Chinese_investment_and_trade">Overall Chinese investment and trade</span></h3>\n<p>Published comments on Kenya\'s <a href="/wiki/98.4_Capital_FM" title="98.4 Capital FM">Capital FM</a> website by Liu Guangyuan, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Ambassador_to_Kenya" title="Chinese Ambassador to Kenya">China\'s ambassador to Kenya</a>, at the time of President Kenyatta\'s 2013 trip to Beijing, said, "Chinese investment in Kenya&#160;... reached $474 million, representing Kenya\'s largest source of foreign direct investment, and&#160;... bilateral trade&#160;... reached $2.84 billion" in 2012. Kenyatta was "[a]ccompanied by 60 Kenyan business people [and hoped to]&#160;... gain support from China for a planned $2.5 billion railway from the southern Kenyan port of Mombasa to neighboring <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, as well as a nearly $1.8 billion dam", according to a statement from the president\'s office also at the time of the trip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp01_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-wp01-105">[105]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Base Titanium, a subsidiary of Base resources of Australia, shipped its first major consignment of minerals to China. About 25,000 tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Ilmenite" title="Ilmenite">ilmenite</a> was flagged off the Kenyan coastal town of Kilifi. The first shipment was expected to earn Kenya about Kshs15&#8211;20 billion in earnings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Recently the Chinese contracted railway project from Nairobi to Mombasa was suspended due to dispute over compensation for land acquisition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vision_2030">Vision 2030</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vision2030_logo.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="663" data-file-width="1525" decoding="async" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Vision2030_logo.svg/220px-Vision2030_logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Vision2030_logo.svg/330px-Vision2030_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Vision2030_logo.svg/440px-Vision2030_logo.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vision2030_logo.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The official logo of <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Vision_2030" title="Kenya Vision 2030">Vision 2030</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2007, the Kenyan government unveiled <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Vision_2030" title="Kenya Vision 2030">Vision 2030</a>, an economic development programme it hopes will put the country in the same league as the <a href="/wiki/Four_Asian_Tigers" title="Four Asian Tigers">Asian Economic Tigers</a> by the year 2030. In 2013, it launched a National Climate Change Action Plan, having acknowledged that omitting climate as a key development issue in Vision 2030 was an oversight. The 200-page Action Plan, developed with support from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_%26_Development_Knowledge_Network" title="Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network">Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network</a>, sets out the Government of Kenya\'s vision for a \'low carbon climate resilient development pathway\'. At the launch in March 2013, the Secretary of the Ministry of Planning, National Development and Vision 2030 emphasised that climate would be a central issue in the renewed Medium Term Plan that would be launched in the coming months. This would create a direct and robust delivery framework for the Action Plan and ensure climate change is treated as an economy-wide issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:90%;">\n<caption style="line-height:1.0em;"><span style="font-size:120%;">Economic summary</span>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">GDP\n</th>\n<td>$41.84&#160;billion (2012) at Market Price. $76.07&#160;billion (Purchasing Power Parity, 2012)\n<p>There exists an informal economy that is never counted as part of the official GDP figures.\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">Annual growth rate\n</th>\n<td>5.1% (2012)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">Per capita income\n</th>\n<td>Per Capita Income (PPP)= $1,800\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">Agricultural&#160;produce<span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;</span>\n</th>\n<td>tea, coffee, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, wheat, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, fruit, vegetables, dairy products, beef, pork, poultry, eggs\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">Industry\n</th>\n<td>small-scale consumer goods (plastic, furniture, batteries, textiles, clothing, soap, cigarettes, flour), agricultural products, horticulture, oil refining; aluminium, steel, lead; cement, commercial ship repair, tourism\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:90%;">\n<caption style="line-height:1.0em;">Trade in 2012\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">Exports\n</th>\n<td>$5.942&#160;billion\n</td>\n<td>tea, coffee, horticultural products, petroleum products, cement, fish\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">Major markets\n</th>\n<td colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> 9.9%, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> 9.6%, Netherlands 8.4%, UK, 8.1%, US 6.2%, Egypt 4.9%, Democratic Republic of the Congo 4.2% (2012)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">Imports\n</th>\n<td>$14.39&#160;billion\n</td>\n<td>machinery and transportation equipment, petroleum products, motor vehicles, iron and steel, resins and plastics\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">Major&#160;suppliers\n</th>\n<td colspan="2">China 15.3%, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> 13.8%, UAE 10.5%, Saudi Arabia 7.3%, South Africa 5.5%, Japan 4.0% (2012)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_exploration">Oil exploration</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Kenya#Petroleum" title="Energy in Kenya">Oil in Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2825" data-file-width="4253" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG/300px-Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG/450px-Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG/600px-Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenya_Aerial_2009-08-27_14-26-44.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lake_Turkana" title="Lake Turkana">Lake Turkana</a> borders Turkana County</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya has proven oil deposits in <a href="/wiki/Turkana_County" title="Turkana County">Turkana County</a>. President Mwai Kibaki announced on 26 March 2012 that <a href="/wiki/Tullow_Oil" title="Tullow Oil">Tullow Oil</a>, an Anglo-Irish oil exploration firm, had struck oil but its commercial viability and subsequent production would take about three years to confirm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Early in 2006 Chinese president <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a> signed an oil exploration contract with Kenya, part of a series of deals designed to keep Africa\'s natural resources flowing to China\'s rapidly expanding economy.\n</p><p>The deal allowed for China\'s state-controlled offshore oil and gas company, <a href="/wiki/China_National_Offshore_Oil_Corporation" title="China National Offshore Oil Corporation">CNOOC</a>, to prospect for oil in Kenya, which is just beginning to drill its first exploratory wells on the borders of Sudan and the disputed area of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Province,_Kenya" title="North Eastern Province, Kenya">North Eastern Province</a> of the border with <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and in coastal waters. There are formal estimates of the possible reserves of oil discovered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Child_labour_and_prostitution">Child labour and prostitution</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="855" decoding="async" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg/300px-Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg/450px-Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg/600px-Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enfants_Masai_-_Kenya_d%C3%A9cembre_1990.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai people</a>. The Maasai live in both Kenya and Tanzania.</div></div></div>\n<p>Child labour is common in Kenya. Most working children are active in agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_&#8211;_Kenya_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_&#8211;_Kenya-150">[150]</a></sup> In 2006, UNICEF estimated that up to 30% of girls in the coastal areas of Malindi, Mombasa, Kilifi, and Diani were subject to prostitution. Most of the prostitutes in Kenya are aged 9&#8211;18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_&#8211;_Kenya_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_&#8211;_Kenya-150">[150]</a></sup> The Ministry of Gender and Child Affairs employed 400 child protection officers in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_&#8211;_Kenya_150-2"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_&#8211;_Kenya-150">[150]</a></sup> The causes of child labour include poverty, the lack of access to education and weak government institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_report_&#8211;_Kenya_150-3"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile_report_&#8211;_Kenya-150">[150]</a></sup> Kenya has ratified Convention No. 81 on labour inspection in industries and Convention No. 129 on labour inspection in agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg/220px-African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg/330px-African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg/440px-African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:African_Kids_working_in_the_family_farm.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Child labour in Kenya</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Microfinance_in_Kenya">Microfinance in Kenya</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Microfinance_in_Kenya" title="Microfinance in Kenya">Microfinance in Kenya</a></div>\n<p>24 institutions offer business loans on a large scale, specific agriculture loans, education loans, and for any other purpose loans. Additionally there are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>emergency loans, which are more expensive in respect to interest rates, but are quickly available</li>\n<li>group loans for smaller groups (4&#8211;5 members) and larger groups (up to 30 members)</li>\n<li>women loans, which are also available to a group of women</li></ul>\n<p>Out of approximately 40 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenyans" title="Kenyans">Kenyans</a>, about 14 million Kenyans are not able to receive financial service through formal loan application service and an additional 12 million Kenyans have no access to financial service institutions at all. Further, 1 million Kenyans are reliant on informal groups for receiving financial aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Conditions for microfinance products</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Eligibility criteria: the general criteria might include gender as in the case for special women loans, to be at least 18 years old, to own a valid Kenyan ID, have a business, demonstrate the ability to repay the loan, and to be a customer of the institution.</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Credit_scoring" title="Credit scoring">Credit scoring</a>: there is no advanced credit scoring system and the majority has not stated any official loan distribution system. However, some institutions require to have an existing business for at least 3 months, own a small amount of cash, provide the institution with a business plan or proposal, have at least one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guarantor" title="Guarantor">guarantor</a>, or to attend group meetings or training. For group loans, almost half of the institutions require group members to guarantee for each other.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Interest_rate" title="Interest rate">Interest rate</a>: they are mostly calculated on a flat basis and some at a declining balance. More than 90% of the institutions require monthly interest payments. The average interest rate is 30&#8211;40% for loans up to 500,000 Kenyan Shilling. For loans above 500,000 Kenyan Shilling, interest rates go up to 71%.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kenya" title="Demographics of Kenya">Demographics of Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg/170px-Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg/255px-Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg/340px-Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kikuyu_woman_traditional_dress.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> <a href="/wiki/Kikuyu_people" title="Kikuyu people">Kikuyu</a> woman in traditional attire</div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-153">[153]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">6.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">31.4\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">48.5\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Kenya had a population of approximately 48 million people in January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">[2]</a></sup> Kenya has a young population, with 73% of residents aged below 30 years because of rapid <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> from 2.9&#160;million to 40&#160;million inhabitants over the last century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenya\'s capital, Nairobi, is home to <a href="/wiki/Kibera" title="Kibera">Kibera</a>, one of the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Shanty_town" title="Shanty town">slums</a>. The shanty town is believed to house between 170,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nation1_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-nation1-157">[157]</a></sup> and 1 million locals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The UNHCR base in <a href="/wiki/Dadaab" title="Dadaab">Dadaab</a> in the north also currently houses around 500,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DadaabPop_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-DadaabPop-159">[159]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_woman_wearing_traditional_tribal_beads_in_Turkana,_Kenya,_October_2012_(8405274783).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4272" data-file-width="2848" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/A_woman_wearing_traditional_tribal_beads_in_Turkana%2C_Kenya%2C_October_2012_%288405274783%29.jpg/170px-A_woman_wearing_traditional_tribal_beads_in_Turkana%2C_Kenya%2C_October_2012_%288405274783%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/A_woman_wearing_traditional_tribal_beads_in_Turkana%2C_Kenya%2C_October_2012_%288405274783%29.jpg/255px-A_woman_wearing_traditional_tribal_beads_in_Turkana%2C_Kenya%2C_October_2012_%288405274783%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/A_woman_wearing_traditional_tribal_beads_in_Turkana%2C_Kenya%2C_October_2012_%288405274783%29.jpg/340px-A_woman_wearing_traditional_tribal_beads_in_Turkana%2C_Kenya%2C_October_2012_%288405274783%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_woman_wearing_traditional_tribal_beads_in_Turkana,_Kenya,_October_2012_(8405274783).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_peoples" title="Nilotic peoples">Nilotic</a> <a href="/wiki/Turkana_people" title="Turkana people">Turkana</a> woman wearing traditional neck beads</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya has a diverse population that includes most major ethnoracial and linguistic groups found in Africa. There are an estimated 47 different communities, with <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantus</a> (67%) and <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_peoples" title="Nilotic peoples">Nilotes</a> (30%) constituting the majority of local residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asongumarr_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asongumarr-160">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> groups also form a small <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_minority" title="Ethnic minority">ethnic minority</a>, as do <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">Arabs</a>, Indians and Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asongumarr_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-Asongumarr-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Okothndaloh_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Okothndaloh-161">[161]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_National_Bureau_of_Statistics" title="Kenya National Bureau of Statistics">Kenya National Bureau of Statistics</a> (KNBS), Kenya has a total population of 38,610,097 inhabitants. The largest native ethnic groups are the <a href="/wiki/Kikuyu_people" title="Kikuyu people">Kikuyu</a> (6,622,576), <a href="/wiki/Luhya_people" title="Luhya people">Luhya</a> (5,338,666), <a href="/wiki/Kalenjin_people" title="Kalenjin people">Kalenjin</a> (4,967,328), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luo_people" title="Luo people">Luo</a> (4,044,440), <a href="/wiki/Kamba_people" title="Kamba people">Kamba</a> (3,893,157), <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalis</a> (3,510,757), <a href="/wiki/Kisii_people" title="Kisii people">Kisii</a> (2,205,669), <a href="/wiki/Mijikenda_peoples" title="Mijikenda peoples">Mijikenda</a> (1,960,574), <a href="/wiki/Meru_people" title="Meru people">Meru</a> (1,658,108), <a href="/wiki/Turkana_people" title="Turkana people">Turkana</a> (988,592), and <a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai</a> (841,622). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Province,_Kenya" title="North Eastern Province, Kenya">North Eastern Province</a> of Kenya, formerly known as NFD, is predominantly inhabited by the indigenous ethnic <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalis</a>. Foreign-rooted populations include <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalis</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>), Kenyan <a href="/wiki/Omanis" title="Omanis">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Kenya" title="Indians in Kenya">Asians</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_people_in_Kenya" title="White people in Kenya">Europeans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Kenya" title="Languages of Kenya">Languages of Kenya</a></div>\n<p>Kenya\'s various ethnic groups typically speak their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" title="Mother tongue">mother tongues</a> within their own communities. The two <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a>, English and <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, are used in varying degrees of fluency for communication with other populations. English is widely spoken in commerce, schooling and government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cugrwed_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cugrwed-163">[163]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peri-urbanisation" title="Peri-urbanisation">Peri-urban</a> and rural dwellers are less multilingual, with many in rural areas speaking only their native languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Broassim_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-Broassim-164">[164]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a> is primarily used in Kenya. Additionally, a distinct local dialect, <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_English" title="Kenyan English">Kenyan English</a>, is used by some communities and individuals in the country, and contains features unique to it that were derived from local <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu languages</a>, such as Kiswahili and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gikuyu_language" title="Gikuyu language">Kikuyu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cliike_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cliike-165">[165]</a></sup> It has been developing since colonisation and also contains certain elements of <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sheng_slang" title="Sheng slang">Sheng</a> is a Kiswahili-based <a href="/wiki/Cant_(language)" title="Cant (language)">cant</a> spoken in some urban areas. Primarily consisting of a mixture of Kiswahili and English, it is an example of linguistic <a href="/wiki/Code-switching" title="Code-switching">code-switching</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nphil_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nphil-166">[166]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are a total of 69 languages spoken in Kenya. Most belong to two broad language families: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niger-Congo_languages" title="Niger-Congo languages">Niger-Congo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu branch</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">Nilo-Saharan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nilotic_languages" title="Nilotic languages">Nilotic branch</a>), spoken by the country\'s Bantu and Nilotic populations, respectively. The Cushitic and Arab ethnic minorities speak languages belonging to the separate <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> family, with the Indian and European residents speaking languages from the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethnken_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnken-167">[167]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_centres">Urban centres</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Kenya_by_population" title="List of cities and towns in Kenya by population">List of cities and towns in Kenya by population</a></div>\n<table Kenya">Name</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Kenya" title="Counties of Kenya">County</a>\n</th>\n<th><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Kenya_by_population" title="List of style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Malindi" title="Malindi">Malindi</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Kilifi_County"
