696\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Kenya" title="Religion in Kenya">Religion in Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG/220px-Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG/330px-Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG/440px-Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catholic_Church_in_Mombasa.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Holy Ghost Roman Catholic cathedral in Mombasa.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mwingi_mosque.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Mwingi_mosque.JPG/220px-Mwingi_mosque.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Mwingi_mosque.JPG/330px-Mwingi_mosque.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Mwingi_mosque.JPG/440px-Mwingi_mosque.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mwingi_mosque.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mosque in <a href="/wiki/Mwingi" title="Mwingi">Mwingi</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The majority of Kenyans are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> (83%), of whom 47.7% are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> and 23.5% are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_Rite" title="Latin Rite">Latin Rite</a> <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Kenya" title="Catholic Church in Kenya">Roman Catholic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KNBS_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-KNBS-168">[168]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_East_Africa" title="Presbyterian Church of East Africa">Presbyterian Church of East Africa</a> has 3 million followers in Kenya and surrounding countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> There are smaller conservative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> churches, the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Evangelical_Presbyterian_Church" title="Africa Evangelical Presbyterian Church">Africa Evangelical Presbyterian Church</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Presbyterian_Church_in_Kenya" title="Independent Presbyterian Church in Kenya">Independent Presbyterian Church in Kenya</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Church_of_East_Africa" title="Reformed Church of East Africa">Reformed Church of East Africa</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" title="Orthodox Christianity">Orthodox Christianity</a> counts 621,200 adherents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Kenya has by far the highest number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quaker" title="Quaker">Quakers</a> of any country in the world, with around 146,300 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_synagogue" title="Jewish synagogue">Jewish synagogue</a> in the country is located in Nairobi.\n</p><p>Islam is the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Kenya" title="Islam in Kenya">second largest religion</a>, comprising 15% of the population. Sixty percent of Kenyan Muslims live in the <a href="/wiki/Coast_Province" title="Coast Province">Coastal Region</a>, comprising 50% of the total population there, while the upper part of Kenya\'s <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Province_(Kenya)" title="Eastern Province (Kenya)">Eastern Region</a> is home to 10% of the country\'s Muslims, where they constitute the majority religious group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" title="African traditional religion">Indigenous beliefs</a> are practiced by 1.7% of the population, although many self-identifying Christians and Muslims <a href="/wiki/Religious_syncretism" title="Religious syncretism">maintain some traditional beliefs and customs</a>. Nonreligious Kenyans make up 2.4% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KNBS_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-KNBS-168">[168]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenya has one of Africa\'s largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> populations (around 300,000), mostly of <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indian</a> origin. It also hosts among the largest number of adherents of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baha%27i_Faith_in_Kenya" title="Baha\'i Faith in Kenya">Baha\'i Faith</a> (430,000), about 1% of the population. There is also a small <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> community.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Kenya" title="Health in Kenya">Health in Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kapsowarhospital1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kapsowarhospital1.jpg/220px-Kapsowarhospital1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kapsowarhospital1.jpg/330px-Kapsowarhospital1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kapsowarhospital1.jpg/440px-Kapsowarhospital1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kapsowarhospital1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Outpatient Department of AIC Kapsowar Hospital<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Kapsowar" title="Kapsowar">Kapsowar</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya\'s <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">private sector</a> is one of the most advanced and dynamic in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>. Private healthcare businesses and companies are the main health care providers in the country even for the nation\'s poorest people. The private health sector is larger and more easily accessible than both the public and the non-profit  health sectors in terms of facilities and personnel. According to a World Bank report, nearly half of the poorest 20 percent of Kenyans use a private health facility when a child is sick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Private health facilities are largely preferred for their strong brands, <a href="/wiki/Value_added" title="Value added">value-addition</a> and focused patient-centered care in contrast to the minimalist evidence-based care provided in public health facilities. Private health facilities are diverse and cater for all economic groups. Hospitals such as the <a href="/wiki/Aga_Khan_University_Hospital,_Nairobi" title="Aga Khan University Hospital, Nairobi">Aga Khan Hospital</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mombasa_Hospital" title="Mombasa Hospital">Mombasa Hospital</a> are comparable to many preferred hospitals in the developed world but are expensive and accessible only to the rich and the insured. Many affordable and low-cost private medical institutions and clinics exist and are easily accessible to ordinary and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle-class" title="Middle-class">middle-class</a> residents but are commonly unregistered and unlicensed and run by similarly unregistered and unlicensed personnel posing a grave danger to the public. All registered medical facilities are subjected to regular supervisory and supportive visits from a joint multi-cadre team of health officials from the county government and national regulatory bodies in order to meet the legal threshold of the <b>Fair Administrative Action Act, 2015</b> and may choose to undergo additional supportive and quality assurance and improvement processes by operating under a social franchise such as the joint government-donor funded <a href="/wiki/Population_Services_International" title="Population Services International">Tunza Family Network</a>.\n</p><p>The control of medical practice by laymen through limited liability companies, county governments and other artificial legal entities is widespread and largely tolerated unlike other countries where medical affairs are strictly handled by medically qualified administrators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The health sector and health facilities are not protected by any special laws and are prone to mismanagement with health workers frequently being subjected to verbal, emotional and physical attacks by patients and administrators alike.\n</p><p>The public health sector consists of community-based (level I) services which are run by community health workers, dispensaries (level II facilities) which are run by nurses, health centers (level III facilities) which are run by clinical officers, sub-county hospitals (level IV facilities) which may be run by a clinical officer or a medical officer, county hospitals (level V facilities) which may be run by a medical officer or a medical practitioner, and national referral hospitals (level VI facilities) which are run by fully qualified medical practitioners (consultants and sub-specialists).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="323" data-file-width="1218" decoding="async" height="58" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png/220px-Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png/330px-Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png/440px-Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Table_rco_co_mo_medical_practitioners.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Table showing different grades of clinical officers, medical officers and medical practitioners in Kenya\'s public service</div></div></div><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurses" title="Nurses">Nurses</a> are by far the largest group of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Front-line" title="Front-line">front-line</a> health care providers in all sectors followed by <a href="/wiki/Clinical_officer" title="Clinical officer">clinical officers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_officer" title="Medical officer">medical officers</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_practitioner" title="Medical practitioner">medical practitioners</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_National_Bureau_of_Statistics" title="Kenya National Bureau of Statistics">Kenya National Bureau of Statistics</a>, in 2011 there were 65,000 qualified nurses registered in the country; 8,600 clinical officers and 7,000 doctors for the population of 43 million people (These figures from official registers include those who have died or left the profession hence the actual number of these workers may be lower).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_healer" title="Traditional healer">Traditional healers</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbalist" title="Herbalist">Herbalists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witch_doctor" title="Witch doctor">witch doctors</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faith_healer" title="Faith healer">faith healers</a>) are readily available, trusted and widely consulted as practitioners of first or last choice by both rural and urban dwellers.\n</p><p>Despite major achievements in the health sector, Kenya still faces many challenges. The <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> estimate has dropped to approximately 55 years in 2009&#8212;five years below 1990 levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> rate is high at approximately 44 deaths per 1,000 children in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> The WHO estimated in 2011 that only 42% of births were attended by a skilled health professional.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Diseases_of_poverty" title="Diseases of poverty">Diseases of poverty</a> directly correlate with a country\'s <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economic performance</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wealth_distribution" title="Wealth distribution">wealth distribution</a>: Half of Kenyans live below the poverty level. Preventable diseases like malaria, HIV/AIDS, pneumonia, diarrhoea and malnutrition are the biggest burden, major child-killers, and responsible for much morbidity; weak policies, corruption, inadequate health workers, weak management and poor leadership in the public health sector are largely to blame. According to 2009 estimates, HIV <a href="/wiki/Prevalence" title="Prevalence">prevalence</a> is about 6.3% of the adult population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> However, the 2011 UNAIDS Report suggests that the HIV epidemic may be improving in Kenya, as HIV prevalence is declining among young people (ages 15&#8211;24) and pregnant women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Kenya had an estimated 15 million cases of <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Kenya" title="Women in Kenya">Women in Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2269" data-file-width="2600" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg/220px-Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg/330px-Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg/440px-Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_Women_in_Nairobi_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenyan women in Nairobi</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> in Kenya is estimated to be 4.49 children per woman in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> According to a 2008&#8211;09 survey by the Kenyan government, the total fertility rate was 4.6% and the contraception usage rate among married women was 46%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" title="Maternal mortality">Maternal mortality</a> is high, partly because of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Female_genital_cutting" title="Female genital cutting">female genital mutilation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_124-4"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-124">[124]</a></sup> with about 27% of women having undergone it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>\nThis practice is however on the decline as the country becomes more modernised, and the practice was also banned in the country in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup>\nWomen were economically empowered before colonialization. \nBy colonial land alienation, women lost access and control of land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> They became more economically dependent on men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> A colonial order of gender emerged where the male dominated the female. \n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup>\nMedian age at first marriage increases with increasing education.\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup>\nRape, defilement and battering are not always seen as serious crimes.\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-192">[192]</a></sup>\nReports of sexual assault are not always taken seriously. \n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-192">[192]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Kenya" title="Education in Kenya">Education in Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg/220px-Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg/330px-Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg/440px-Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Community_work_in_Kenya_DVIDS342488.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>School children in a classroom.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg/220px-MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg/330px-MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg/440px-MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MSc_student_at_Kenyatta_University.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An MSc student at <a href="/wiki/Kenyatta_University" title="Kenyatta University">Kenyatta University</a> in Nairobi.</div></div></div>\n<p>Children attend nursery school, or kindergarten in the private sector until they are five years old. This lasts one to three years (KG1, KG2 and KG3) and is financed privately because there has been no government policy regarding it until recently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Basic formal education starts at age six years and lasts 12 years consisting of eight years in primary school and four years in high school or secondary school. Primary school is free in public schools and those attending can join a vocational youth/village polytechnic or make their own arrangements for an apprenticeship program and learn a trade such as tailoring, carpentry, motor vehicle repair, brick-laying and masonry for about two years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-194">[194]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Those who complete high school can join a <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">polytechnic</a> or other technical college and study for three years, or proceed directly to the university and study for four years. Graduates from the polytechnics and colleges can then join the workforce and later obtain a specialized higher diploma qualification after a further one to two years of training, or join the university&#8212;usually in the second or third year of their respective course. The <a href="/wiki/Higher_diploma" title="Higher diploma">higher diploma</a> is accepted by many employers in place of a bachelor\'s degree and direct or accelerated admission to post-graduate studies is possible in some universities.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="886" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg/220px-Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg/330px-Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg/440px-Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Masai_girl_at_school_doing_maths.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Maasai girl at school.</div></div></div>\n<p>Public universities in Kenya are highly commercialized institutions and only a small fraction of qualified high school graduates are admitted on limited government-sponsorship into programs of their choice. Most are admitted into the social sciences, which are cheap to run, or as self-sponsored students paying the full cost of their studies. Most qualified students who miss out opt for middle-level diploma programs in public or private universities, colleges, and polytechnics.\n</p><p>38.5 percent of the Kenyan adult population is illiterate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> There are very wide regional disparities; for example, Nairobi had the highest level of literacy, 87.1 per cent, compared to North Eastern Province, the lowest, at 8.0 per cent. Preschool, which targets children from age three to five, is an integral component of the education system and is a key requirement for admission to Standard One (First Grade). At the end of primary education, pupils sit the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Certificate_of_Primary_Education" title="Kenya Certificate of Primary Education">Kenya Certificate of Primary Education</a> (KCPE), which determines those who proceed to secondary school or vocational training.  The result of this examination is needed for placement at secondary school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_194-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-194">[194]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Primary school is for students aged 6/7-13/14 years. For those who proceed to the secondary level, there is a national examination at the end of Form Four&#160;&#8211; the <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education" title="Kenya Certificate of Secondary Education">Kenya Certificate of Secondary Education</a> (KCSE), which determines those proceeding to the universities, other professional training or employment. Students sit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Examinations" title="Examinations">examinations</a> in eight subjects of their choosing. However, English, Kiswahili and mathematics are compulsory subjects.\n</p><p>The Kenya Universities and Colleges Central Placement Service (KUCCPS), formerly the Joint Admissions Board (JAB),  is responsible for selecting students joining the public universities. Other than the public schools, there are many private schools, mainly in urban areas. Similarly, there are a number of <a href="/wiki/International_school" title="International school">international schools</a> catering to various overseas educational systems.\n</p><p>Despite its impressive commercial approach and interests in the country, Kenya\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academia" title="Academia">academia</a> and higher education system is notoriously rigid and disconnected from the needs of the local labour market and is widely blamed for the high number of unemployable and "half-baked" university graduates who struggle to fit in the modern workplace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kenya" title="Culture of Kenya">Culture of Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_dancers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1089" data-file-width="1384" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kenyan_dancers.jpg/220px-Kenyan_dancers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kenyan_dancers.jpg/330px-Kenyan_dancers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kenyan_dancers.jpg/440px-Kenyan_dancers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kenyan_dancers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenyan boys and girls performing a traditional dance</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nation_media_house.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="851" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nation_media_house.jpg/220px-Nation_media_house.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nation_media_house.jpg/330px-Nation_media_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Nation_media_house.jpg/440px-Nation_media_house.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nation_media_house.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nation Media House which hosts the <a href="/wiki/Nation_Media_Group" title="Nation Media Group">Nation Media Group</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kenya" title="Culture of Kenya">culture of Kenya</a> consists of multiple traditions. Kenya has no single prominent culture that identifies it. It instead consists of the various cultures of the country\'s different communities.\n</p><p>Notable populations include the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili</a> on the coast, several other <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> communities in the central and western regions, and Nilotic communities in the northwest. The <a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai</a> culture is well known to tourism, despite constituting a relatively small part of Kenya\'s population. They are renowned for their elaborate upper body adornment and jewellery.\n</p><p>Additionally, Kenya has an extensive music, television and theater scene.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Kenya" title="Media of Kenya">Media of Kenya</a></div>\n<p>Kenya has a number of media outlets that broadcast domestically and globally. They cover news, business, sports and entertainment.\nPopular Kenyan newspapers include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Nation" title="Daily Nation">The Daily Nation</a></i>; part of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_Media_Group" title="Nation Media Group">Nation Media Group (NMG)</a> (largest market share)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Standard_(Kenya)" title="The Standard (Kenya)">The Standard</a></i></li>\n<li><i>The Star</i></li>\n<li><i>The People</i></li>\n<li><i>East Africa Weekly</i></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Taifa_Leo" title="Taifa Leo">Taifa Leo</a></i></li></ul>\n<p>Television stations based in Kenya include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kenya_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Kenya Broadcasting Corporation">Kenya Broadcasting Corporation</a> (KBC)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Citizen_TV" title="Citizen TV">Citizen TV</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kenya_Television_Network" title="Kenya Television Network">Kenya Television Network</a> (KTN)</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NTV_(Kenya)" title="NTV (Kenya)">NTV</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_Media_Group" title="Nation Media Group">Nation Media Group</a> (NMG))</li>\n<li>Kiss Television</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/K24_(Kenya)" title="K24 (Kenya)">K24 Television</a></li>\n<li>Kass-TV</li></ul>\n<p>All of these terrestrial channels are transmitted via a DVB T2 digital TV signal.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_literature" title="Kenyan literature">Kenyan literature</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_(signing_autographs_in_London).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="485" data-file-width="591" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg/220px-Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg/330px-Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg/440px-Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_%28signing_autographs_in_London%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o_(signing_autographs_in_London).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenyan author <a href="/wiki/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o" title="Ng&#361;g&#297; wa Thiong\'o">Ng&#361;g&#297; wa Thiong\'o</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o" title="Ng&#361;g&#297; wa Thiong\'o">Ng&#361;g&#297; wa Thiong\'o</a> is one of the best known writers of Kenya. His novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Weep_Not,_Child" title="Weep Not, Child">Weep Not, Child</a></i>, is an illustration of life in Kenya during the British occupation. The story details the effects of the Mau Mau on the lives of Kenyans. Its combination of themes&#8212;<a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>, education, and love&#8212;helped to make it one of the best-known novels in Africa.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M.G._Vassanji" title="M.G. Vassanji">M.G. Vassanji</a>\'s 2003 novel <i>The In-Between World of Vikram Lall</i> won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scotiabank_Giller_Prize" title="Scotiabank Giller Prize">Giller Prize</a> in 2003. It is the fictional memoir of a Kenyan of Indian heritage and his family as they adjust to the changing political climates in colonial and post-colonial Kenya.\n</p><p>Since 2003, the literary journal <i><a href="/wiki/Kwani%3F" title="Kwani?">Kwani?</a></i> has been publishing Kenyan contemporary literature. Additionally, Kenya has also been nurturing emerging versatile authors such as Paul Kipchumba (Kipwendui, Kibiwott) who demonstrate pan-African outlook (see <i>Africa in China\'s 21st Century: In Search of a Strategy</i> (2017).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Kenya" title="Music of Kenya">Music of Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Juacali_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Juacali_2.jpg/220px-Juacali_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Juacali_2.jpg/330px-Juacali_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Juacali_2.jpg/440px-Juacali_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Juacali_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Popular Kenyan musician <a href="/wiki/Jua_Cali" title="Jua Cali">Jua Cali</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya has a diverse assortment of popular music forms, in addition to multiple types of <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> based on the variety over 40 regional languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The drums are the most dominant <a href="/wiki/Musical_instrument" title="Musical instrument">instrument</a> in popular Kenyan music. Drum beats are very complex and include both native rhythm and imported ones, especially the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> <a href="/wiki/Cavacha" title="Cavacha">cavacha</a> rhythm. Popular Kenyan music usually involves the interplay of multiple parts, and more recently, showy guitar solos as well. There are also a number of local hip-hop artists, including <a href="/wiki/Jua_Cali" title="Jua Cali">Jua Cali</a> and afro-pop bands such as <a href="/wiki/Sauti_Sol" title="Sauti Sol">Sauti Sol</a>.\n</p><p>Lyrics are most often in Kiswahili or English. There is also some emerging aspect of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lingala_language" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a> borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> musicians. Lyrics are also written in local languages. Urban radio generally only plays English music, though there also exist a number of vernacular radio stations.\n</p><p>Zilizopendwa is a genre of local urban music that was recorded in the 1960s, 70s and 80s by musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Daudi_Kabaka" title="Daudi Kabaka">Daudi Kabaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fadhili_William" title="Fadhili William">Fadhili William</a> and Sukuma Bin Ongaro, and is particularly revered and enjoyed by older people&#8212;having been popularised by the Kenya Broadcasting Corporation\'s Kiswahili service (formerly called Voice of Kenya or VOK).\n</p><p>The isukuti is a vigorous dance performed by the <a href="/wiki/Luhya_people" title="Luhya people">Luhya</a> sub-tribes to the beat of a traditional drum called the Isukuti during many occasions such as the birth of a child, marriage and funerals. Other traditional dances include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohangla" title="Ohangla">Ohangla</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Luo_peoples" title="Luo peoples">Luo</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nzele&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nzele (page does not exist)">Nzele</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Mijikenda_peoples" title="Mijikenda peoples">Mijikenda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mugithi" title="Mugithi">Mugithi</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Kikuyu_people" title="Kikuyu people">Kikuyu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taarab" title="Taarab">Taarab</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili</a>.\n</p><p>Additionally, Kenya has a growing Christian gospel music scene. Prominent local gospel musicians include the <a href="/wiki/Kenyan_Boys_Choir" title="Kenyan Boys Choir">Kenyan Boys Choir</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Benga_music" title="Benga music">Benga music</a> has been popular since the late 1960s, especially in the area around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a>. The word <i>benga</i> is occasionally used to refer to any kind of pop music. Bass, guitar and percussion are the usual instruments.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Kenya" title="Sport in Kenya">Sport in Kenya</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg/220px-2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg/330px-2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg/440px-2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2012_Olympics_-_Womens_5000m_start_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jepkosgei Kipyego and Jepkemoi Cheruiyot at London 2012 Olympics 5,000 meters</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya is active in several sports, among them <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rallying" title="Rallying">rallying</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>. The country is known chiefly for its dominance in <a href="/wiki/Middle-distance_running" title="Middle-distance running">middle-distance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long-distance_running" title="Long-distance running">long-distance</a> athletics, having consistently produced Olympic and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> champions in various distance events, especially in 800&#160;m, 1,500&#160;m, 3,000&#160;m steeplechase, 5,000&#160;m, 10,000&#160;m and the marathon. Kenyan athletes (particularly <a href="/wiki/Kalenjin_people" title="Kalenjin people">Kalenjin</a>) continue to dominate the world of distance running, although competition from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> has reduced this supremacy. Kenya\'s best-known athletes included the four-time women\'s <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon" title="Boston Marathon">Boston Marathon</a> winner and two-time world champion <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Ndereba" title="Catherine Ndereba">Catherine Ndereba</a>, 800m world record holder <a href="/wiki/David_Rudisha" title="David Rudisha">David Rudisha</a>, former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marathon_(sport)" title="Marathon (sport)">Marathon</a> world record-holder <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tergat" title="Paul Tergat">Paul Tergat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Ngugi" title="John Ngugi">John Ngugi</a>.\n</p><p>Kenya won several medals during the Beijing Olympics, six gold, four silver and four bronze, making it Africa\'s most successful nation in the 2008 Olympics. New athletes gained attention, such as <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Jelimo" title="Pamela Jelimo">Pamela Jelimo</a>, the women\'s 800m gold medalist who went on to win the <a href="/wiki/IAAF_Golden_League" title="IAAF Golden League">IAAF Golden League</a> jackpot, and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Wanjiru" title="Samuel Wanjiru">Samuel Wanjiru</a> who won the men\'s marathon. Retired Olympic and Commonwealth Games champion <a href="/wiki/Kipchoge_Keino" title="Kipchoge Keino">Kipchoge Keino</a> helped usher in Kenya\'s ongoing distance dynasty in the 1970s and was followed by Commonwealth Champion <a href="/wiki/Henry_Rono" title="Henry Rono">Henry Rono</a>\'s spectacular string of world record performances. Lately, there has been controversy in Kenyan athletics circles, with the defection of a number of Kenyan athletes to represent other countries, chiefly <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IAAF_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-IAAF-199">[199]</a></sup> The Kenyan Ministry of Sports has tried to stop the defections, but they have continued anyway, with <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Lagat" title="Bernard Lagat">Bernard Lagat</a> the latest, choosing to represent the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IAAF_199-1"><a href="#cite_note-IAAF-199">[199]</a></sup> Most of these defections occur because of economic or financial factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> Decisions by the Kenyan government to tax athletes\' earnings may also be a reason for defection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Some elite Kenyan runners who cannot qualify for their country\'s strong national team find it easier to qualify by running for other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg/220px-David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg/330px-David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg/440px-David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_Rudisha_Daegu_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenyan Olympic and world record holder in the 800 meters, <a href="/wiki/David_Rudisha" title="David Rudisha">David Rudisha</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenya has been a dominant force in women\'s volleyball within Africa, with both the clubs and the national team winning various continental championships in the past decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> The women\'s team has competed at the Olympics and <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Women\'s World Championship">World Championships</a> though without any notable success. Cricket is another popular sport, also ranking as the most successful team sport. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenyan_cricket_team" title="Kenyan cricket team">Kenya</a> has competed in the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cup</a> since <a href="/wiki/1996_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1996 Cricket World Cup">1996</a>. They upset some of the world\'s best teams and reached the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2003_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2003 Cricket World Cup">2003 tournament</a>. They won the inaugural World Cricket League Division 1 hosted in Nairobi and participated in the World T20. They also participated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICC_Cricket_World_Cup_2011" title="ICC Cricket World Cup 2011">ICC Cricket World Cup 2011</a>. Their current captain is <a href="/wiki/Rakep_Patel" title="Rakep Patel">Rakep Patel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenya is represented by <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Onyango" title="Lucas Onyango">Lucas Onyango</a> as a professional rugby league player who plays with the English club <a href="/wiki/Oldham_R.L.F.C." title="Oldham R.L.F.C.">Oldham</a>. Besides the former <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> team, he has played for the <a href="/wiki/Widnes_Vikings" title="Widnes Vikings">Widnes Vikings</a> and rugby union with the <a href="/wiki/Sale_Sharks" title="Sale Sharks">Sale Sharks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> Rugby union is increasing in popularity, especially with the annual <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Safaricom_Sevens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Safaricom Sevens (page does not exist)">Safari Sevens</a> tournament. The <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_rugby_sevens_team" title="Kenya national rugby sevens team">Kenya Sevens team</a> ranked 9th in IRB Sevens World Series for the 2006 season. In 2016, the team beat Fiji at the Singapore Sevens finals, making Kenya the second African nation after South Africa to win a World Series championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_football_team" title="Kenya national football team">Kenya</a> was also a regional powerhouse in football. However, its dominance has been eroded by wrangles within the now defunct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenya_Football_Federation" title="Kenya Football Federation">Kenya Football Federation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> leading to a suspension by <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> which was lifted in March 2007.\n</p><p>In the motor rallying arena, Kenya is home to the world-famous <a href="/wiki/Safari_Rally" title="Safari Rally">Safari Rally</a>, commonly acknowledged as one of the toughest rallies in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> It was a part of the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">World Rally Championship</a> for many years until its exclusion after the 2002 event owing to financial difficulties. Some of the best rally drivers in the world have taken part in and won the rally, such as <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Waldeg%C3%A5rd" title="Bj&#246;rn Waldeg&#229;rd">Bj&#246;rn Waldeg&#229;rd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hannu_Mikkola" title="Hannu Mikkola">Hannu Mikkola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tommi_M%C3%A4kinen" title="Tommi M&#228;kinen">Tommi M&#228;kinen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shekhar_Mehta" title="Shekhar Mehta">Shekhar Mehta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Sainz" title="Carlos Sainz">Carlos Sainz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colin_McRae" title="Colin McRae">Colin McRae</a>. Although the rally still runs annually as part of the Africa rally championship, the organisers are hoping to be allowed to rejoin the World Rally championship in the next couple of years.\n</p><p>Nairobi has hosted several major continental sports events, including the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa_Championship_1993" title="FIBA Africa Championship 1993">FIBA Africa Championship 1993</a> where <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_basketball_team" title="Kenya national basketball team">Kenya\'s national basketball team</a> finished in the top four, its best performance to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="576" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg/220px-Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg/330px-Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg/440px-Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ugali_%26_Sukuma_Wiki.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ugali" title="Ugali">Ugali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sukuma_wiki" title="Sukuma wiki">sukuma wiki</a>, staples of Kenyan cuisine</div></div></div>\n<p>Kenyans generally have three meals in a day&#8212;breakfast in the morning (<i>kiamsha kinywa</i>), lunch in the afternoon (<i>chakula cha mchana</i>) and supper in the evening (<i>chakula cha jioni</i> or known simply as "chajio"). In between, they have the 10 o\'clock tea (<i>chai ya saa nne</i>) and 4&#160;p.m. tea (<i>chai ya saa kumi</i>). Breakfast is usually tea or porridge with bread, <a href="/wiki/Chapati" title="Chapati">chapati</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahamri" title="Mahamri">mahamri</a>, boiled sweet potatoes or <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">yams</a>. <a href="/wiki/Githeri" title="Githeri">Githeri</a> is a common lunch time dish in many households while <a href="/wiki/Ugali" title="Ugali">Ugali</a> with vegetables, sour milk (<a href="/wiki/Mursik" title="Mursik">Mursik</a>), meat, fish or any other stew is generally eaten by much of the population for lunch or supper. Regional variations and dishes also exist.\n</p><p>In western Kenya: among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luo_(Kenya_and_Tanzania)" title="Luo (Kenya and Tanzania)">Luo</a>, fish is a common dish; among the <a href="/wiki/Kalenjin_people" title="Kalenjin people">Kalenjin</a> who dominate much of the Rift Valley Region, <a href="/wiki/Mursik" title="Mursik">mursik</a>&#8212;sour milk&#8212;is a major drink.\n</p><p>In cities such as <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, there are fast food restaurants, including <a href="/wiki/Steers" title="Steers">Steers</a>, <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> There are also many fish and chip shops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kenya" title="Foreign relations of sanitation in Kenya</a></li></ul>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint metadata navbox" role="navigation" style="font-weight:bold;padding:0.4em 2em"><ul style="margin:0.1em 0 0"><li
